t.map((e=>e.replace(/["']/g,"")))}extractAPICall(e,t){const i=new RegExp(t+"\\((.*?)\\)","g"),o=e.match(i);return null!==o&&o[0]}disableAllAds(e){e&&!x(e)||(this.all=!0,this.reasons.add("all_page"))}disableContentAds(e){e&&!x(e)||(this.content=!0,this.recipe=!0,this.locations.add(c.Content),this.locations.add(c.Recipe),this.reasons.add("content_plugin"))}disablePlaylistPlayers(e){e&&!x(e)||(this.video=!0,this.locations.add("Video"),this.reasons.add("video_page"))}urlHasEmail(e){if(!e)return!1;return null!==/([A-Z0-9._%+-]+(@|%(25)*40)[A-Z0-9.-]+\.[A-Z]{2,})/i.exec(e)}constructor(e){this.adthrive=e,this.all=!1,this.content=!1,this.recipe=!1,this.video=!1,this.locations=new Set,this.reasons=new Set,(this.urlHasEmail(window.location.href)||this.urlHasEmail(window.document.referrer))&&(this.all=!0,this.reasons.add("all_email"));try{this.checkCommandQueue(),null!==document.querySelector(".tag-novideo")&&(this.video=!0,this.locations.add("Video"),this.reasons.add("video_tag"))}catch(e){C.error("ClsDisableAds","checkCommandQueue",e)}}}const I=window.adthriveCLS;return I&&(I.disableAds=new A(window.adthrive)),e.ClsDisableAds=A,e}({});
</script>		<style id="wp-custom-css">

    margin-bottom: 1em;

	<div id="primary" class="content-area primary">

		
					<main id="main" class="site-main">
				

<article
class="post-3120 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-graphic-design ast-article-single" id="post-3120" itemtype="https://schema.org/CreativeWork" itemscope="itemscope">

	
	
<div class="ast-post-format- single-layout-1">

	
	
		<header class="entry-header ">

			
			<p class="ast-terms-link"><a href="https://www.color-meanings.com/category/graphic-design/" class="">Graphic Design</a></p><h1 class="entry-title" itemprop="headline">134 Shades of Green: Color Names, Hex, RGB, CMYK Codes</h1>
			
		</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	
	
	<div class="entry-content clear"
	itemprop="text"	>

		
		
<figure class="wp-block-image"><img decoding="async" width="940" height="788" src="https://www.color-meanings.com/wp-content/uploads/shades-of-green-color-names.png" alt="Shades of Green Color with Names and HTML, Hex, RGB Codes" class="wp-image-3207" srcset="https://www.color-meanings.com/wp-content/uploads/shades-of-green-color-names.png 940w, https://www.color-meanings.com/wp-content/uploads/shades-of-green-color-names-300x251.png 300w, https://www.color-meanings.com/wp-content/uploads/shades-of-green-color-names-768x644.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 940px) 100vw, 940px" /></figure>



<p>Most people would agree that there are seven colors in a rainbow, and one of them is green. But how boring would life be if we only had seven colors to choose from and weren&#8217;t allowed to combine colors together?</p>



<p>Luckily, the world isn&#8217;t that limited. There are thousands of colors out there, many of which are shades of one particular hue. Not to mention that the shades of green being used have grown substantially over the years, with some variations having only existed since the late 1800s.</p>



<p>Whether you&#8217;re looking for a specific shade you vaguely remember or need to find matching colors for your design or website, there are almost endless options. Below are a variety of green shades with their names, Hex, RGB, and CMYK codes.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Forest Green</h2>



<p>We all know what forest green looks like; it&#8217;s a rich, deep color that reminds one of Evergreen trees. It&#8217;s a nice shade if you&#8217;re looking for a darker color for your design.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#0b6623"><strong>Forest green</strong><br>Hex #0B6623<br>RGB 11, 102, 35<br>CMYK 89, 0, 66, 60</p><p>
<script async data-uid="fa6a8b44df" src="https://colormeanings.kit.com/fa6a8b44df/index.js"></script>
</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Olive</h2>



<p>A color you may recognize if you&#8217;re familiar with olives, like those infamous fruits (yes olives are fruits) we all know and either love or hate. Olive green shouldn&#8217;t need much description for you to picture what it looks like.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#708238"><strong>Olive</strong><br>Hex #708238<br>RGB 112, 130, 56<br>CMYK 14, 0, 57, 49</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Hunter Green</h2>



<p>Hunter green is a pale green. It&#8217;s a mellow color that reminds one of a forest floor near the end of autumn; the grass isn&#8217;t vibrant at this time of year and because of this lack of vibrancy, the grass can look pale. That&#8217;s what hunter green can be described as.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#3f704d"><strong>Hunter green</strong><br>Hex #3F704D<br>RGB 63, 112, 77<br>CMYK 44, 0, 31, 56</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Artichoke Green</h2>



<p>You may be thinking that artichoke green has to look and have the exact same color as its aforementioned namesake, but artichokes are slightly brighter than this color. Artichoke green can look a little pale when you first see it, about a mix between gray and green, but incorporate it in your design and you&#8217;ll find yourself staring at a soothing green color that can complement every element and style that exists.</p><p><a href="https://www.color-meanings.com/color-personality-quiz/"><img decoding="async" class="alignnone wp-image-43119 size-full" src="https://www.color-meanings.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/12/color-personality-quiz.gif" alt="Color personality quiz animation" width="920" height="518" /></a></p>




<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#8f9779"><strong>Artichoke green</strong><br>Hex #8F9779<br>RGB 143, 151, 121<br>CMYK 5, 0, 20, 41</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Jungle Green</h2>



<p>Jungle green is another color that you may think you already know the looks of without seeing it, but when you discover it, you realize that it&#8217;s entirely different. Jungle green is a hard color to describe as the color can be all over the place, since there are even variations of jungle green itself. These include tropical rainforest, amazon, deep jungle green, medium jungle green, and dark jungle green. If you don&#8217;t like the look of jungle green itself, color codes for the other shades are included below. Jungle green is used in the United States Army for the color of the uniforms and berets that are worn by the United States Army Special Forces.</p>



<p>Because jungle green is such a rich and versatile color, it can be utilized for almost everything.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#29ab87"><strong>Jungle green<br></strong>Hex #29AB87<br>RGB 41, 171, 135<br>CMYK 76, 0, 21, 33</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#00755e"><strong>Tropical Rainforest<br></strong>Hex #00755E<br>RGB 0, 117, 94<br>CMYK 100, 0, 20, 54</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#3b7a57"><strong>Amazon</strong><br>Hex #3B7A57<br>RGB 59, 122, 87<br>CMYK 52, 0, 29, 52</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#004b49"><strong>Deep Jungle green<br></strong>Hex #004B49<br>RGB 0, 75, 73<br>CMYK 100, 0, 3, 71</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#1c352d"><strong>Medium Jungle green<br></strong>Hex #1C352D<br>RGB 28, 53, 45<br>CMYK 47, 0, 15, 79</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#1a2421"><strong>Dark Jungle green<br></strong>Hex #1A2421<br>RGB 26, 36, 33<br>CMYK 28, 0, 8, 86</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Moss Green</h2>



<p>A color that is slightly similar to its namesake, as moss green resembles the coloration that you see in moss.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#8a9a5b"><strong>Moss green</strong><br>Hex #8A9A5B<br>RGB 138, 154, 91<br>CMYK 10, 0, 41, 40</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Myrtle Green</h2>



<p>As much as one would think that myrtle green is the appropriate word to describe the color Moaning Myrtle from the Harry Potter series living face would have taken if she needed to barf (yes, I&#8217;m a huge HP fan), this color is anything but that. Myrtle green is meant to represent the unique color that are the leaves of a myrtle plant. Myrtle is a genus of flowering plants that are native to the Mediterranean region of southern Europe as well as North Africa.</p>



<p>If you need an idea of what myrtle green might look like, the modern cricket caps worn by Australian test cricketers are dyed myrtle green.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#317873"><strong>Myrtle green</strong><br>Hex #317873<br>RGB 49, 120, 115<br>CMYK 59, 0, 4, 53</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Pine Green</h2>



<p>Pine green is what you would think it looks like. It&#8217;s a rich color and a shade of spring green that is akin to the color of pine trees. It has been an official color in the Crayola company since 1903.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#01796f"><strong>Pine green</strong><br>Hex #01796F<br>RGB 1, 121, 111<br>CMYK 99, 0, 8, 53</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Persian Green</h2>



<p>Persian green is a unique color that doesn&#8217;t tend to be used often. It&#8217;s a color that is typically seen in Persian carpets and pottery. It&#8217;s a color that you can find all over Iran due to its positive connotation, as the color is renowned for representing nature, heaven, and sanctity.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#00a693"><strong>Persian green</strong><br>Hex #00A693<br>RGB 0, 166, 147<br>CMYK 100, 0, 11, 35</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Emerald Green</h2>



<p>Emerald green is one of those unique colors that has been featured a lot in popular culture, from Ireland&#8217;s nickname as the&nbsp;<em>Emerald Isle</em>&nbsp;due to the countries abundance of lush greenery, to the infamous city in&nbsp;<em>The Wonderful Wizard of Oz</em> where Dorthy encounters that not only is the food emerald green, but so are the people. Emerald green is a shade of green that isn&#8217;t particularly light or bright, as the color is similar to the appearance of an emerald gemstone.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#50c878"><strong>Emerald green</strong><br>Hex #50C878<br>RGB 80, 200, 120<br>CMYK 60, 0, 40, 22</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Neon Green</h2>



<p>Neon green is a very bright shade of green that is primarily seen in psychedelic art, fashion, or if you&#8217;ve ever had laser lights in a club flash directly into your eyes, then you have an idea of what this color looks like.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#39ff14"><strong>Neon green</strong><br>Hex #39FF14<br>RGB 57, 255, 20<br>CMYK 78, 0, 92, 0</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Sacramento Green</h2>



<p>Aptly named because of its use as the official color for California&#8217;s Sacramento State University. While this color might not see much use outside of the official capacity for the college, it&#8217;s a variation of green that you should know exist.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#043927"><strong>Sacramento green</strong><br>Hex #043927<br>RGB 4, 57, 39<br>CMYK 93, 0, 32, 78</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Sea Green</h2>



<p>Sea green is a color that resembles the seafloor, which is then reflected through the water. So if you&#8217;ve ever gone swimming at a beach and found that the water had a green tinge to it, that effect is caused by sea green.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#2e8b57"><strong>Sea green</strong><br>Hex #2E8B57<br>RGB 46, 139, 87<br>CMYK 67, 0, 37, 45</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Sage Green</h2>



<p>This is a greenish-gray color that resembles the color of dried sage leaves.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#9dc183"><strong>Sage green</strong><br>Hex #9DC183<br>RGB 157, 193, 131<br>CMYK 19, 0, 32, 24</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Lime Green</h2>



<p>Lime green is a color that resembles the color of the fruit, lime. It&#8217;s bright and vivid in coloration.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#c7ea46"><strong>Lime green</strong><br>Hex #C7EA46<br>RGB 199, 234, 70<br>CMYK 15, 0, 70, 8</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Jade Green</h2>



<p>Jade green got its name due to the fact that its color closely resembles that of the jade gemstone, despite the fact that the hue of jades themselves can vary widely.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#00a86b"><strong>Jade green</strong><br>Hex #00A86B<br>RGB 0, 168, 107<br>CMYK 100, 0, 36, 34</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Fern Green</h2>



<p>Fern green got its name as the color closely resembles fern leaves. In 1998, Crayola officially included fern green into their products, though it tends to be fairly lighter than the official color swatches for fern green.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#4f7942"><strong>Fern green</strong><br>Hex #4F7942<br>RGB 79, 121, 66<br>CMYK 35, 0, 45, 53</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Laurel Green</h2>



<p>While laurel green sounds like it could be the name of a country singer with several platinum records to her name, laurel green is anything but that. It&#8217;s a medium-light hue of greenish-gray, similar in color to asparagus, but lighter than that.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#a9ba9d"><strong>Laurel green</strong><br>Hex #A9BA9D<br>RGB 169, 186, 157<br>CMYK 9, 0, 16, 27</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Mint Green</h2>



<p>Mint green is a color that you will discover if you like mint chocolate chip ice cream. Mint green gets its name because it shares a similar color with the mint leaf.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#98fb98"><strong>Mint green</strong><br>Hex #98FB98<br>RGB 152, 251, 152<br>CMYK 39, 0, 39, 2</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Tea Green</h2>



<p>A light shade of green that gets its name from the color of brewed green tea.&nbsp;</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#d0f0c0"><strong>Tea green</strong><br>Hex #D0F0C0<br>RGB 208, 240, 192<br>CMYK 13, 0, 20, 6</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Army Green</h2>



<p>Army green is a color that has been used in militaries since World War II or even before that period, although the hue of army green in military uniforms varies between nations.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#4b5320"><strong>Army green</strong><br>Hex #4B5320<br>RGB 75, 83, 32<br>CMYK 10, 0, 61, 67</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Kelly Green</h2>



<p>Kelly green is a unique color that only seems to exist in America and was coined back in the early 1900s. Kelly green refers to the fact that the surname Kelly, along with the color green, are both popular in Ireland. Due to the fact that much of America&#8217;s early history was made up by the abundance of Irish immigrants, the name grew to popularity in America.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#4cbb17"><strong>Kelly green</strong><br>Hex #4CBB17<br>RGB 76, 187, 23<br>CMYK 59, 0, 88, 27</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Russian Green</h2>



<p>Russian green has a similar history to some other variations of green that appear in this list. It got the name Russian green when it started being used as the shade of green worn by many regiments of the Imperial Russian Army, from 1700 to 1914.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#679267"><strong>Russian green</strong><br>Hex #679267<br>RGB 103, 146, 103<br>CMYK 29, 0, 29, 43</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Paris Green</h2>



<p>Paris green has a lengthy range. It can be pale or even a vivid bluish-green, to a deeper shade of regular green itself. Paris green gets its name from the popular pigment that appeared in artists&#8217; paints and was primarily found in inorganic compound copper acetoarsenite.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#50c878"><strong>Paris green</strong><br>Hex #50C878<br>RGB 80, 200, 120<br>CMYK 60, 0, 40, 22</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Pakistan Green</h2>



<p>Pakistan green is a dark shade of green that is primarily used in web development and graphic design. It gets the name from its use as the background color of the Pakistani flag.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#006600"><strong>Pakistan green</strong><br>Hex #006600<br>RGB 0, 102, 0<br>CMYK 100, 0, 100, 60</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Midnight Green</h2>



<p>Midnight green is a relatively dark, green-bluish color. It&#8217;s the official primary color of the Philadelphia Eagles, which is why it&#8217;s also sometimes referred to as eagle green.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#004953"><strong>Midnight green</strong><br>Hex #004953<br>RGB 0, 73, 83<br>CMYK 100, 12, 0, 67</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">India Green</h2>



<p>India green gets its name from its official use as the color of the lower band of the flag of India. The color is used in the flag to represent fertility and prosperity.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#138808"><strong>India green</strong><br>Hex #138808<br>RGB 19, 136, 8<br>CMYK 86, 0, 94, 47</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Hunter Green</h2>



<p>Hunter green is a color that was mostly worn by hunters in the 1800s. However, most hunters changed and took to wearing olive-colored garbs rather than anything with hunter green by the 1900s. Today, some hunters still wear clothing or bandanas in hunter green.</p>



<p>Hunter green is the official primary color of the Green Bay Packers, as well as the New York Jets from a period of 1998 to 2019.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#355e3b"><strong>Hunter green</strong><br>Hex #355E3B<br>RGB 53, 94, 59<br>CMYK 44, 0, 37, 63</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Celadon</h2>



<p>Celadon is a shade of green that is grayish and pale in nature. It&#8217;s named after a class of Chinese ceramics that made its way to Korea and Japan. Because Celadon has European linguistic roots, its name may have been derived from a character, Celadon, that appears in the work L&#8217;Astre, a French pastoral novel that depicts life in an idealized manner for the reader. The character in the novel wore a light green color.</p>



<p>In the past, Celadon was used as a glaze in pottery; it was fairly common in Asia for its resemblance to jade.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#ace1af"><strong>Celadon</strong><br>Hex #ACE1AF<br>RGB 172, 225, 175<br>CMYK 24, 0, 22, 12</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Avocado</h2>



<p>This is a lovely, deep green that isn&#8217;t quite as dark as the skin of most avocados. However, if you want to inspire a sense of calm and even evoke the peace of a forest, this is a great color to choose for your next project.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#568203"><strong>Avocado</strong><br>Hex #568203<br>RGB 86, 130, 3<br>CMYK 34, 0, 98, 49</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Harlequin</h2>



<p>If you like a neon, in-your-face green, this bright and exciting color is an excellent choice. While its highlighter-like glow may be too much for some projects, it&#8217;s ideal for applications where grabbing attention is absolutely essential.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#3fff00"><strong>Harlequin</strong><br>Hex #3FFF00<br>RGB 63, 255, 0<br>CMYK 75, 0, 100, 0&nbsp;</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Spring</h2>



<p>Spring is the season of new beginnings, and this delicate, pale green captures the idea well. Reminiscent of very new shoots and unfolding leaves, it&#8217;s ideal if you want a lighter green that isn&#8217;t quite a pastel.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#00f0a8"><strong>Spring</strong><br>Hex #00F0A8<br>RGB 0, 240, 168<br>CMYK 100, 0, 30, 6</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Kaitoke</h2>



<p>This deep green is reminiscent of vast forests, which seems appropriate. It&#8217;s named for the Kaitoke Regional Park in New Zealand. For a darker green that still has a lot of energy to it, Kaitoke is an excellent choice.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#004830"><strong>Kaitoke</strong><br>Hex #004830<br>RGB 0, 72, 48<br>CMYK 100, 0, 33, 72</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Screamin&#8217; Green</h2>



<p>From the name, you&#8217;d probably guess that Screamin&#8217; Green is a neon color. However, while it&#8217;s fairly bright, it hasn&#8217;t quite reached neon level. This color is a lot like seafoam green with a bit less blue.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#76ff7a"><strong>Screamin&#8217; Green</strong><br>Hex #76FF7A<br>RGB 118, 255, 122<br>CMYK 54, 0, 52, 0</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Chateau</h2>



<p>This dignified green makes a beautiful wall color if you prefer the slightly darker look. Paler and lighter than olive, Chateau also looks very nice when lightened to a paler green tint.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#48a860"><strong>Chateau</strong><br>Hex #48A860<br>RGB 72, 168, 96<br>CMYK 57, 0, 43, 34</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Dark Moss Green</h2>



<p>If you&#8217;re looking for a deeper green that approaches the level of a neutral color, Dark Moss Green might be your answer. At first glance, this brownish green looks unremarkable. But it offers a quiet elegance that makes it perfect for a backdrop, or even for a text color against a cream white background.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#4a5d23"><strong>Dark Moss Green</strong><br>Hex #4A5D23<br>RGB 74, 93, 35<br>CMYK 20, 0, 62, 64</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Swamp</h2>



<p>Let&#8217;s face it, most of us probably aren&#8217;t jumping to get a color called &#8220;Swamp.&#8221; But if you can get past the drab name, Swamp is actually a pleasant gray-green that can be used as a neutral color in most applications.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#a8c090"><strong>Swamp</strong><br>Hex #A8C090<br>RGB 168, 192, 144<br>CMYK 13, 0, 25, 25</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Mantis</h2>



<p>If you&#8217;ve ever been transfixed by the beauty of a praying mantis, you might appreciate this interesting green shade. Mantis is close to being a pale hunter green, and it&#8217;s a good middle-of-the-road green shade. Not too light, not too dark.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#74c365"><strong>Mantis</strong><br>Hex #74C365<br>RGB 116, 195, 101<br>CMYK 41, 0, 48, 24&nbsp;</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Fun</h2>



<p>You might expect a green called &#8220;fun&#8221; to be a bright, neon-like shade. However, this green is surprisingly somewhat dark. It&#8217;s roughly between a forest and hunter green. If you&#8217;re looking for a nice dark green, this one is certainly an option.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#007848"><strong>Fun</strong><br>Hex #007848<br>RGB 0, 120, 72<br>CMYK 100, 0, 40, 53</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Pantone Artichoke Green</h2>



<p>Distinct from Artichoke Green, this color comes from Pantone, the world-renowned color-matching company. Its grayish-green shade does get close to the color of the outside of an artichoke, too.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#4b6f44"><strong>Pantone Artichoke Green</strong><br>Hex #4B6F44<br>RGB 75, 111, 68<br>CMYK 32, 0, 39, 56</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Viridian</h2>



<p>Bluish greens tend to inspire a sense of calm, and Viridian does just that. This deep and peaceful green looks a lot like the ocean on a cloudy day. Its grayish quality makes it close to being a neutral, but not quite.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#609078"><strong>Viridian</strong><br>Hex #609078<br>RGB 96, 144, 120<br>CMYK 33, 0, 17, 44</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Reseda Green</h2>



<p>This interesting shade is similar to Russian Green, but it&#8217;s a bit darker. It gets its name from the plant Reseda odorata, and it is included as part of Germany&#8217;s RAL color standard.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#6c7c59"><strong>Reseda Green</strong><br>Hex #6C7C59<br>RGB 108, 124, 89<br>CMYK 13, 0, 28, 51&nbsp;</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Chetwode</h2>



<p>Chetwode is a pale, barely-there green, but it&#8217;s perfectly balanced. As you can see from the RGB values, it has almost equal amounts of blue and green. And if you&#8217;re wondering about the unusual name, Chetwode has the same name as a small village in England.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#f0fff0"><strong>Chetwode</strong><br>Hex #F0FFF0<br>RGB 240, 255, 240<br>CMYK 6, 0, 6, 0</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Shamrock Green</h2>



<p>We all know of the shamrock, a good-luck charm and symbol of Ireland. And while most shamrocks have a bit more yellow in them than this green does, this shamrock green is nonetheless a pretty, sprightly green that can add some life to your project.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#009e60"><strong>Shamrock Green</strong><br>Hex #009E60<br>RGB 0, 158, 96<br>CMYK 100, 0, 39, 38&nbsp;</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Verdun</h2>



<p>Verdun is a city in northern France, and it&#8217;s also the name of this interesting dark green. Despite its depth, Verdun manages to still be fairly energetic. This is thanks to its high yellow CMYK value. However, the relatively high amounts of black and blue stop it from becoming overly bright.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#487800"><strong>Verdun</strong><br>Hex #487800<br>RGB 72, 120, 0<br>CMYK 40, 0, 100, 53</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Castleton Green</h2>



<p>This green is the official color of Castleton University in Vermont. It&#8217;s a bluish pine green with a stately air to it, and it looks especially nice against white. If you&#8217;re looking for a bluish twist on a classic color, this is a great option.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#00563b"><strong>Castleton Green</strong><br>Hex #00563B<br>RGB 0, 86, 59<br>CMYK 100, 0, 31, 66</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Gin</h2>



<p>This pleasantly pale green looks a bit like a diluted form of the color of juniper, the plant used to make gin. It&#8217;s a grayish, almost khaki green that&#8217;s ideal if you want just a touch of a neutral-like green.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#d8e4bc"><strong>Gin</strong><br>Hex #D8E4BC<br>RGB 216, 228, 188<br>CMYK 5, 0, 18, 11</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Granny Smith Apple</h2>



<p>Just about everyone is familiar with the tart crispness of the classic Granny Smith apple. This slightly demure green, while it&#8217;s a bit less yellow than most Granny Smiths, is nonetheless a great tribute. It&#8217;s ideal if you like mint-like greens but want something slightly darker.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#a8e4a0"><strong>Granny Smith Apple</strong><br>Hex #A8E4A0<br>RGB 168, 228, 160<br>CMYK 26, 0, 30, 11</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Bitter Lime</h2>



<p>Bitter Lime is an interesting twist on the classic lime green. And just like an actual lime that&#8217;s on the tart side, this color has more yellow than blue. The result is an unusual color, but it&#8217;s great for applications like advertising when you want a bright color without going to a near-blinding neon shade.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#bfff00"><strong>Bitter Lime</strong><br>Hex #BFFF00<br>RGB 191, 255, 0<br>CMYK 25, 0, 100, 0</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Bright Mint</h2>



<p>Like Bitter Lime, Bright Mint is a twist on a classic green shade. Specifically, Bright Mint is a little more blue and a little brighter. The result is something that looks like a cross between turquoise and seafoam green. If you need a color that&#8217;s eye-catching without being overwhelming, this is a great answer.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#4fffb0"><strong>Bright Mint</strong><br>Hex #4FFFB0<br>RGB 79, 255, 176<br>CMYK 69, 0, 31, 0</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Bottle Green</h2>



<p>As the name suggests, this color is similar to that of a dark green glass bottle (and especially close to the color of an older bottle). It&#8217;s another bluish green, but it leans more to the blue side (as evidenced by the 100% cyan value).</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#006a4e"><strong>Bottle Green</strong><br>Hex #006A4E<br>RGB 0, 106, 78<br>CMYK 100, 0, 26, 58</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Cadmium Green</h2>



<p>Cadmium Green, sometimes also called Empire, is a bold and confident shade that&#8217;s just a bit lighter than hunter green. It&#8217;s deep without being overly dark, making it a well-balanced choice for most projects.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#006b3c"><strong>Cadmium Green</strong><br>Hex #006B3C<br>RGB 0, 107, 60<br>CMYK 100, 0, 44, 58</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Camouflage Green</h2>



<p>There are practically as many camouflage patterns as there are terrains. But Camouflage Green (or a very close color) can be found in most. This is a unique, bluish-gray green that works as a neutral. It makes an excellent, quiet wall color, and it also looks nice in a lighter tint.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#78866b"><strong>Camouflage Green</strong><br>Hex #78866B<br>RGB 120, 134, 107<br>CMYK 10, 0, 20, 47</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Pear</h2>



<p>This pleasant yellow-green is almost exactly the color of a ripe Bartlett pear. Thanks to the K value (black), it&#8217;s a little quieter than many yellow greens. If you want to evoke a spring-like atmosphere in your project, this is a great shade of green to consider.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#d1e231"><strong>Pear</strong><br>Hex #D1E231<br>RGB 209, 226, 49<br>CMYK 8, 0, 78, 11</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Dollar Bill</h2>



<p>The color green is commonly associated with money, and Dollar Bill is a color that gets close to the green on the dollar bill. Its sage-like color gives it a classic, understated look, and it&#8217;s especially pretty in paler tints.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#85bb65"><strong>Dollar Bill</strong><br>Hex #85BB65<br>RGB 133, 187, 101<br>CMYK 29, 0, 46, 27</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Inchworm</h2>



<p>As a child, you might have noticed these bright yellow-green bugs inching slowly along in springtime. This cheerful bright green is slightly softened by a bit of black, making it a well-balanced shade that&#8217;s ideal for a range of different projects.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#b2ec5d"><strong>Inchworm</strong><br>Hex #B2EC5D<br>RGB 178, 236, 93<br>CMYK 25, 0, 61, 7</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Asparagus</h2>



<p>This sage-like green isn&#8217;t really the color of asparagus, but it&#8217;s nonetheless a classic, beautiful color that&#8217;s well-suited to a variety of uses. Asparagus is slightly muted, and it pairs well with soft pinks and purples.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#87a96b"><strong>Asparagus</strong><br>Hex #87A96B<br>RGB 135, 169, 107<br>CMYK 20, 0, 37, 34</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Caribbean Green</h2>



<p>Caribbean Green is just barely a green. Like the bright, clear waters of the Caribbean, this color is more of a blue with a hint of green. It&#8217;s a great way to help create the idea of a warm, summery atmosphere.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#00cc99"><strong>Caribbean Green</strong><br>Hex #00CC99<br>RGB 0, 204, 153<br>CMYK 100, 0, 25, 20</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">GO Green</h2>



<p>This standout shade of green looks a bit like the needles of a blue spruce tree. It&#8217;s a medium green in color, but its slight blue cast makes it a bit different from most colors on the list.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#00ab66"><strong>GO Green</strong><br>Hex #00AB66<br>RGB 0, 171, 102<br>CMYK 100, 0, 40, 33</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Phthalo Green</h2>



<p>This oddly-named color is a synthetic green pigment that&#8217;s frequently used to make oil and acrylic paints. Among the ingredients for the pigment are copper and the chemical phthalocyanine, which is where the name comes from. This deep green is almost exactly the same color as the pigment itself.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#123524"><strong>Phthalo Green</strong><br>Hex #123524<br>RGB 18, 53, 36<br>CMYK 66, 0, 32, 79</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Napier Green</h2>



<p>This is an interesting bright-green color with a high amount of yellow. If you know about supercars, you might recognize the color as one that is sometimes used on McLaren cars. If you need a high-energy color similar to Kelly Green, Napier Green is a good one to look into.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#2a8000"><strong>Napier Green</strong><br>Hex #2A8000<br>RGB 42, 128, 0<br>CMYK 67, 0, 100, 50</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Feldgrau</h2>



<p>If you&#8217;re a history buff, Feldgrau may look familiar. This grayish green color was the official color of the uniforms of German soldiers from the early 1900s to the 1940s. If you need a stately gray with just a hint of green, Feldgrau is a good color to choose.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#4d5d53"><strong>Feldgrau</strong><br>Hex #4D5D53<br>RGB 77, 93, 83<br>CMYK 17, 0, 11, 64</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Green-Yellow</h2>



<p>Green-Yellow doesn&#8217;t have a very exciting name. But the name does describe the color perfectly: it&#8217;s a greenish yellow. As you can see from the CMYK values, it leans more yellow than blue, creating a bright and high-energy hue.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#adff2f"><strong>Green-Yellow</strong><br>Hex #ADFF2F<br>RGB 173, 255, 47<br>CMYK 32, 0, 82, 0</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Malachite</h2>



<p>This beautifully balanced color is what most people likely picture when they imagine green. Though it has slightly more blue than yellow, Malachite offers a classic green that may well be the right color for your project.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#0bda51"><strong>Malachite</strong><br>Hex #0BDA51<br>RGB 11, 218, 81<br>CMYK 95, 0, 63, 15</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Rifle Green</h2>



<p>This deep olive green gets its name from the fact that it (or colors like it) is sometimes used as the uniform color for rifle regiments. It&#8217;s an ideal choice if you need a darker color but don&#8217;t want to go for the more typical black or plain dark gray.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#444c38"><strong>Rifle Green</strong><br>Hex #444C38<br>RGB 68, 76, 56<br>CMYK 11, 0, 26, 70</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Volt</h2>



<p>Even the name of this color suggests high energy. And as you may have guessed, Volt is one of the yellowest greens on the list. With a yellow value of 100 and a cyan value of 19, its brightness is tempered just enough. Still, if you need a shock of near-yellow for your project, Volt is certainly an option.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#ceff00"><strong>Volt</strong><br>Hex #CEFF00<br>RGB 206, 255, 0<br>CMYK 19, 0, 100, 0</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">British Racing Green</h2>



<p>As you&#8217;ve likely figured out from the name, British Racing Green is the official color of the United Kingdom&#8217;s motor racing. It&#8217;s a deep green that looks a lot like both hunter and forest greens.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#004225"><strong>British Racing Green</strong><br>Hex #004225<br>RGB 0, 66, 37<br>CMYK 100, 0, 44, 74</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Thyme</h2>



<p>The name of this shade of green is somewhat deceptive. While it&#8217;s close to the shade of natural thyme, it has a bit more yellow. Still, it&#8217;s a versatile color that&#8217;s similar to Kelly Green.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#5edc1f"><strong>Thyme</strong><br>Hex #5EDC1F<br>RGB 94, 220, 31<br>CMYK 57, 0, 86, 14</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Chartreuse</h2>



<p>This bright greenish-yellow is named after a green or yellow French liqueur that has been made since the 1700s. It&#8217;s a great option if you are looking for an almost-neon shade of green.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#7fff00"><strong>Chartreuse</strong><br>Hex #7FFF00<br>RGB 127, 255, 0<br>CMYK 50, 0, 100, 0</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Corn Green</h2>



<p>Most of us likely don&#8217;t think of corn when we imagine the color green. However, this dusky greenish-yellow is just about the exact color of the leaves that cover an ear of corn. If you need a shade of green that&#8217;s light and yellow-heavy without being overly bright, this is a great candidate.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#71a92c"><strong>Corn Green</strong><br>Hex #71A92C<br>RGB 113, 169, 44<br>CMYK 33, 0, 74, 34</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Shrek Green</h2>



<p>Many shades of green are named after things in nature, but Shrek Green gets its name from the popular animated ogre. It&#8217;s an unusual mixture of yellow-green and olive, but if you want something that breaks the mold, it&#8217;s a great choice.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#c4d300"><strong>Shrek Green</strong><br>Hex #C4D300<br>RGB 196, 211, 0<br>CMYK 7, 0, 100, 17</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Christmas Green</h2>



<p>If you need a color to commemorate the most wonderful time of the year, Christmas Green is it. It&#8217;s bright yet deep, and it&#8217;s just about the exact shade of green icing you&#8217;d make to decorate Christmas tree cookies.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#00873e"><strong>Christmas Green</strong><br>Hex #00873E<br>RGB 0, 135, 62<br>CMYK 100, 0, 54, 47</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Irish Green</h2>



<p>From green fields to shamrocks to the green bar on the flag, green has long been a color associated with Ireland. Irish Green is a balanced and pleasantly energetic color that&#8217;s ideal for use if you want a classic green that&#8217;s more blue than yellow.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#009a44"><strong>Irish Green</strong><br>Hex #009A44<br>RGB 0, 154, 68<br>CMYK 100, 0, 56, 40</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Road Sign Green</h2>



<p>This relaxed blue-green is meant to resemble the colors of some road signs. As you can see from CMYK values, it leans heavily blue as opposed to yellow. This makes it a better choice if your project features primarily cool colors, or if you need a cooler color to balance out a too-hot color scheme.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#01735c"><strong>Road Sign Green</strong><br>Hex #01735C<br>RGB 1, 115, 92<br>CMYK 99, 0, 20, 55</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Lightsaber Green</h2>



<p>This lively green is similar to both Harlequin and Chartreuse. If you need a neon green that&#8217;s so bright it glows, Lightsaber Green just might be your answer. It looks especially striking against pure black or deep blue.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#2ff924"><strong>Lightsaber Green</strong><br>Hex #2FF924<br>RGB 47, 249, 36<br>CMYK 81, 0, 86, 2</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Girl Scout Green</h2>



<p>If you&#8217;ve ever bought Girl Scout cookies, then you&#8217;re familiar with the green and white logo for the Girl Scouts. But even for other design purposes, this classic and distinguished green is a wise choice. Pair it with white for an elegant look, or pair it with pale pink to make it really pop.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#00ae58"><strong>Girl Scout Green</strong><br>Hex #00AE58<br>RGB 0, 174, 88<br>CMYK 100, 0, 49, 32</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Tennis Court Green</h2>



<p>Any tennis player, casual or serious, will immediately recognize this shade of green. Its sage-like color looks great with white, but it also serves as a useful backdrop for brighter colors and pastels.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#6c935c"><strong>Tennis Court Green</strong><br>Hex #6C935C<br>RGB 108, 147, 92<br>CMYK 27, 0, 37, 42</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Spring Bud</h2>



<p>We&#8217;re all familiar with the thin, yellow-green leaf buds that signal the start of spring. This high-energy green captures that color beautifully. Though not as green as Chartreuse or Harlequin, it&#8217;s still useful for adding a pop of color to your project.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#a7fc00"><strong>Spring Bud</strong><br>Hex #A7FC00<br>RGB 167, 252, 0<br>CMYK 34, 0, 100, 1</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Chinese Green</h2>



<p>This unusual green looks, at first glance, more like a yellow-brown. However, it has an almost jewel-tone look to it, and it pairs well with deep reds. While Chinese Green likely would not be considered a true neutral, it&#8217;s somewhat close.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#d0db61"><strong>Chinese Green</strong><br>Hex #D0DB61<br>RGB 208, 219, 97<br>CMYK 5, 0, 56, 14</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Arctic Lime</h2>



<p>If you pay attention to color trends, you may have noticed that colors like Arctic Lime are making a comeback. Arctic Lime has some characteristics of neon, but it&#8217;s not quite as bright, making it generally more pleasing to the eye. It looks especially dramatic against stark black.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#d0ff14"><strong>Arctic Lime</strong><br>Hex #D0FF14<br>RGB 208, 255, 20<br>CMYK 18, 0, 92, 0</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Nyanza</h2>



<p>Named after a city in Rwanda, Nyanza is a beautifully soft mint green. If you like pastels, it makes an especially soothing wall color. It also works as an alternative to white if you&#8217;re selecting background colors. Nyanza would also work well in a watercolor-esque, pastel color palette.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#e9ffdb"><strong>Nyanza</strong><br>Hex #E9FFDB<br>RGB 233, 255, 219<br>CMYK 9, 0, 14, 0</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Dark Lemon-Lime</h2>



<p>When you think of lemon-lime, you probably picture a slightly brighter, yellower shade. This medium green simply offers a little more lime than it does lemon.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#76ba1b"><strong>Dark Lemon-Lime</strong><br>Hex #76BA1B<br>RGB 118, 186, 27<br>CMYK 37, 0, 85, 27</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Crayola Yellow-Green</h2>



<p>This color, which is in similar vein to lemon-lime, is the same color as Crayola&#8217;s yellow-green crayon. It&#8217;s sure to bring back memories of coloring as a child. Crayola Yellow-Green is roughly the shade of grass as it begins to yellow. And thanks to the fact that it has very little black, it manages to be bright without becoming overpowering.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#acdf87"><strong>Crayola Yellow-Green</strong><br>Hex #ACDF87&nbsp;<br>RGB 172, 223, 135<br>CMYK 23, 0, 39, 13</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Maximum Green</h2>



<p>Like a few other shades on the list, Maximum Green is close to the classic idea of green most people have in their heads. It&#8217;s a bright, strong green with just enough depth, and it works well in a variety of applications. And as you can see from the RGB values, the presence of green dramatically outshines both red and blue.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#4c9a2a"><strong>Maximum Green</strong><br>Hex #4C9A2A<br>RGB 76, 154, 42<br>CMYK 51, 0, 73, 40</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Vivid Lime Green</h2>



<p>Lime green is more than just one shade. From Arctic Lime to Vivid Lime Green, you can find it in seemingly endless iterations. Vivid Lime Green has a high percentage of yellow, but it has enough black to add some depth. Compared to some more fluorescent types of lime, Vivid Lime Green has a bit more presence.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#a4de02"><strong>Vivid Lime Green</strong><br>Hex #A4DE02<br>RGB 164, 222, 2<br>CMYK 26, 0, 99, 13</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Pistachio</h2>



<p>This color is named after everyone&#8217;s favorite green nut, and it&#8217;s about the color of pistachio ice cream. It&#8217;s a great choice if you want a medium-light green that isn&#8217;t overly bright. Since it&#8217;s tempered by black, this shade of green is a little muted, although not as much as the various shades of olive green.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#93c572"><strong>Pistachio</strong><br>Hex #93C572<br>RGB 147, 197, 114<br>CMYK 25, 0, 42, 23</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Medium Spring Green</h2>



<p>Medium Spring Green is an especially lovely spring green. It manages to be both soft and bright, and it looks almost like a slightly darker mint-green pastel. It can be easy to mix up the various shades of spring green, but this is one that really shouldn&#8217;t get lost in the shuffle.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#00fa9a"><strong>Medium Spring Green</strong><br>Hex #00FA9A<br>RGB 0, 250, 154<br>CMYK 100, 0, 38, 2</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Sheen Green</h2>



<p>This oddly-named color looks like an interesting mix between moss green and spring green. It&#8217;s easy on the eyes and looks especially nice as a backdrop for black text. It gets its name from the Sheen Green crayon by Crayola.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#8fd400"><strong>Sheen Green</strong><br>Hex #8FD400<br>RGB 143, 212, 0<br>CMYK 33, 0, 100, 17</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">La Salle Green</h2>



<p>This bold green is the official color of the La Salle Greenies. This is the varsity team at La Salle Green Hills, a school in the Philippines. In the NCAA, the Greenies are the junior affiliate team of the St. Benilde Blazers.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#087830"><strong>La Salle Green</strong><br>Hex #087830<br>RGB 8, 120, 48<br>CMYK 93, 0, 60, 53</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Spanish Viridian</h2>



<p>This bluish-green color is a variant of Viridian, mentioned earlier. However, Spanish Viridian is a bit more green (as opposed to blue) than the generic Viridian.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#007f5c"><strong>Spanish Viridian</strong><br>Hex #007F5C&nbsp;<br>RGB 0, 127, 92<br>CMYK 100, 0, 28, 50</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Dartmouth Green</h2>



<p>Many colleges have colors involving some form of dark green. This particular shade is the official green of Dartmouth College, an Ivy League college in New Hampshire. The official Dartmouth colors are white and Dartmouth Green. Side-by-side with white, Dartmouth Green creates a pleasing contrast. Though not as loud as some other collegiate colors, this deep green is incredibly elegant.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#00703c"><strong>Dartmouth Green</strong><br>Hex #00703C<br>RGB 0, 112, 60<br>CMYK 100, 0, 46, 56</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Pine Needle Color</h2>



<p>Every so often, you run across a shade of green whose name doesn&#8217;t really seem to match up. Pine Needle Color is one of those shades. It&#8217;s much more brown than you might expect. Its deep, dark color is partially explained by the high percentage of black compared to yellow and green. If you want a neutral color that has some green in it, the unusual Pine Needle Color is worth considering.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#454d32"><strong>Pine Needle Color</strong><br>Hex #454D32<br>RGB 69, 77, 50<br>CMYK 10, 0, 35, 70</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Olive Drab</h2>



<p>Despite its unappealing name, Olive Drab is actually a fairly nice color. It&#8217;s slightly lighter than many olive shades, and it&#8217;s just about exactly the color of a manzanilla olive. If you like olive greens but want one you don&#8217;t see too often, Olive Drab is a good choice.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#6b8e23"><strong>Olive Drab</strong><br>Hex #6B8E23<br>RGB 107, 142, 35<br>CMYK 25, 0, 75, 44</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Lawn Green</h2>



<p>Lawn Green is somewhat close to Chartreuse in color, making it a lot brighter than many people&#8217;s lawns. However, it&#8217;s close to the color of grass when it&#8217;s illuminated by falling light. This is a good color to choose if you like the lightness of spring greens and pastels but want something that&#8217;s a bit more energizing.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#7cfc00"><strong>Lawn Green</strong><br>Hex #7CFC00<br>RGB 124, 252, 0<br>CMYK 51, 0, 100, 1</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Xanadu</h2>



<p>At first glance, Xanadu looks more like slate gray than any shade of green. However, as you can see by RGB values, it still does have a relatively high proportion of green. But thanks to also having a good bit of black (as shown in the CMYK values), Xanadu has a largely gray appearance. If you&#8217;re looking for a distinctive, uncommon neutral, this is a great one to consider.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#738678"><strong>Xanadu</strong><br>Hex #738678<br>RGB 115, 134, 120<br>CMYK 14, 0, 10, 47</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Dark Olive Green</h2>



<p>When it comes to choosing a shade of green, types of olive are generally popular. Olive is understated yet elegant, and it comes close to being a neutral color. Dark Olive Green is an excellent option. It looks especially nice with various shades of yellow, and it fits in well with neutrals like gray and tan.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#556b2f"><strong>Dark Olive Green</strong><br>Hex #556B2F<br>RGB 85, 107, 47<br>CMYK 21, 0, 56, 58</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Dark Sea Green</h2>



<p>This color is roughly the shade of the ocean on a cloudy day. It&#8217;s also an excellent uncommon color to choose for a project. Most of us are familiar with sea green, but it&#8217;s fairly common, especially around the summertime. This variant can let your work stand out. And thanks to its relatively high degree of blue and black, it&#8217;s very much at home in a cooler color palette.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#8fbc8f"><strong>Dark Sea Green</strong><br>Hex #8FBC8F<br>RGB 143, 188, 143<br>CMYK 24, 0, 24, 26</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Green (Munsell)</h2>



<p>This color is a green featured by the Munsell Color Company. The company was founded by Albert H. Munsell, developer of Munsell Color Theory. Munsell&#8217;s Color System focused on the chroma, value, and hue of different colors. &#8220;Chroma&#8221; refers to intensity, &#8220;value&#8221; refers to lightness, and &#8220;hue&#8221; refers to the basic color. This green has a good bit of blue, giving it a pleasing, cool cast.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#00a877"><strong>Green (Munsell)</strong><br>Hex #00A877<br>RGB 0, 168, 119<br>CMYK 100, 0, 29, 34</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Mughal Green</h2>



<p>Mughal Green is a shade of green with ancient and royal connections. It&#8217;s named for the flag of the Mughal Empire that ruled northern India in the sixteenth, seventeenth, and eighteenth centuries. The flag features a dark green backdrop with a sun and golden lion in the foreground. It&#8217;s outlined in deep red.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#306030"><strong>Mughal Green</strong><br>Hex #306030<br>RGB 48, 96, 48<br>CMYK 50, 0, 50, 62</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">John Deere Green</h2>



<p>John Deere Green is iconic, especially in rural America. It&#8217;s the official color used on tractors and mowers made by John Deere. John Deere Green is an interesting shade. It&#8217;s somewhere between Kelly Green and Hunter Green. As you may have gathered from seeing the John Deere logo, it looks especially nice when paired with bright yellow.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#367c2b"><strong>John Deere Green</strong><br>Hex #367C2B<br>RGB 54, 124, 43<br>CMYK 56, 0, 65, 51</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Office Green</h2>



<p>Office Green looks similar to John Deere Green, even though the name would suggest that it&#8217;s best for the indoors as opposed to outdoors. Office Green is one of the most balanced greens on the list. As you can see by the CMYK values, it contains an exactly equal amount of blue and yellow, and then it&#8217;s darkened by the presence of black.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#008000"><strong>Office Green</strong><br>Hex #008000<br>RGB 0, 128, 0<br>CMYK 100, 0, 100, 50</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Limerick</h2>



<p>This whimsically-named green looks fairly similar to many of the yellow-greens and lemon-limes on the list. Like Irish Green, it inspires images of rolling hills and sunlight, as it&#8217;s a grassy green with a fair bit of yellow. If you like the various shades of lime on the list but want something a bit darker and less fluorescent, Limerick is a color you may want to consider.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#9dc209"><strong>Limerick</strong><br>Hex #9DC209<br>RGB 157, 194, 9<br>CMYK 19, 0, 95, 24</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Maximum Green Yellow</h2>



<p>If Limerick is the color of grass, then Maximum Green Yellow is the color of dried, yellowed grass in winter. It&#8217;s an unusual shade that looks a bit like an olive green with a significant amount of yellow added. Due to its almost-golden appearance, it pairs very well with deeper shades of blue.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#d9e650"><strong>Maximum Green Yellow</strong><br>Hex #D9E650<br>RGB 217, 230, 80<br>CMYK 6, 0, 65, 10</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">French Lime</h2>



<p>As you&#8217;ve seen, many of the shades of lighter green have names involving lime. And while it might seem like this one is named after a species of lime native to France, that&#8217;s not the case. This shade appears on several French color lists where it&#8217;s simply called &#8220;lime.&#8221; So to differentiate it from the many other shades of lime, it was called &#8220;French Lime.&#8221;</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#9efd38"><strong>French Lime</strong><br>Hex #9EFD38<br>RGB 158, 253, 56<br>CMYK 38, 0, 78, 1</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Medium Spring Bud</h2>



<p>Not to be confused with Medium Spring Green, Medium Spring Bud is a color that looks roughly like a lightened combination of olive and sage. As you can see from its CMYK values, there&#8217;s far more yellow than there is blue or black. Medium Spring Bud is designed to be about the same color as a bud getting ready to bloom.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#c9dc87"><strong>Medium Spring Bud</strong><br>Hex #C9DC87<br>RGB 201, 220, 135<br>CMYK 9, 0, 39, 14</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">UFO Green</h2>



<p>It isn&#8217;t really clear why this color is called UFO Green. After all, there&#8217;s nothing particularly otherworldly about it. In fact, it looks a lot like green grass. But if you&#8217;re looking for a somewhat bright, relatively balanced green with slightly more blue than yellow, UFO Green is a good choice.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#3cd070"><strong>UFO Green</strong><br>Hex #3CD070<br>RGB 60, 208, 112<br>CMYK 71, 0, 46, 18</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Acid Green</h2>



<p>At first glance, Acid Green looks a lot like Olive Drab. It&#8217;s another olive-like green that&#8217;s significantly lightened up by yellow. For a real-world reference, this color is fairly similar to the color of pea soup.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#b0bf1a"><strong>Acid Green</strong><br>Hex #B0BF1A<br>RGB 176, 191, 26<br>CMYK 8, 0, 86, 25</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Chlorophyll Green</h2>



<p>Chlorophyll allows plants to take energy from light, and it&#8217;s a key part of photosynthesis. And since chlorophyll is a green pigment, it makes sense that a shade of green would be named after it. Chlorophyll Green is a bright color similar to neon green.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#4aff00"><strong>Chlorophyll Green</strong><br>Hex #4AFF00<br>RGB 74, 255, 0<br>CMYK 71, 0, 100, 0</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Green Lizard</h2>



<p>When it comes to naming green colors, there&#8217;s no shortage of plants and animals for inspiration. This color, Green Lizard, is roughly the color of an anole, which is a small green lizard. Though Green Lizard is fairly bright, it stops short of being neon, making it much easier to look at.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#a7f432"><strong>Green Lizard</strong><br>Hex #A7F432<br>RGB 167, 244, 50<br>CMYK 32, 0, 80, 4</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Iguana Green</h2>



<p>Here&#8217;s another color named after a green lizard &#8211; Iguana Green. Iguana Green is a little bit more muted, and it has more blue and more black. It&#8217;s remarkably close to the color of an actual iguana.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#71bc78"><strong>Iguana Green</strong><br>Hex #71BC78<br>RGB 113, 188, 120<br>CMYK 40, 0, 36, 26</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Kombu Green</h2>



<p>Kombu Green is easily one of the darkest greens on the list. It&#8217;s named after kombu, a form of edible kelp. As you can see from its CMYK value, Kombu Green has a very high percentage of black compared to other colors.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#354230"><strong>Kombu Green</strong><br>Hex #354230<br>RGB 53, 66, 48<br>CMYK 20, 0, 27, 74</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Middle Green</h2>



<p>Sometimes, a project just needs a middle-of-the-road green. That&#8217;s where the appropriately-named Middle Green can help. It has very similar amounts of blue and yellow (though slightly more blue), and it&#8217;s a balanced shade with a calming effect.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#4d8c57"><strong>Middle Green</strong><br>Hex #4D8C57&nbsp;<br>RGB 77, 140, 87<br>CMYK 45, 0, 38, 45</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Paolo Veronese Green</h2>



<p>This lovely, cool blue-green is named after Paolo Veronese, a renowned Renaissance painter. He was also known as Paolo Caliari, and his most famous paintings include&nbsp;<em>The Feast in the House of Levi</em>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<em>The Wedding at Cana</em>. The color is frequently described as being like Viridian but with additional blue.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#009b7d"><strong>Paolo Veronese Green</strong><br>Hex #009B7D<br>RGB 0, 155, 125<br>CMYK 100, 0, 19, 39</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Pullman Green</h2>



<p>When you first look at Pullman Green, you might think it&#8217;s simply a very dark brown. However, it&#8217;s actually an incredibly deep olive color. The name comes from the Pullman Company, a railroad car manufacturer that operated during the American railroad boom. Its cars were painted this very deep olive green. Originally, the cars were painted chocolate brown. Once the official color was changed to Pullman Green (originally called Brewster Green), the cars continued to be painted in Pullman Green until the company went out of business.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#3b331c"><strong>Pullman Green</strong><br>Hex #3B331C<br>RGB 59, 51, 28<br>CMYK 0, 14, 53, 77</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Green Screen</h2>



<p>Most of us know the green screen as a backdrop of promise. After filming, fantastical backgrounds can be added. This color is just like that of an actual green screen. It&#8217;s a pleasing green in its own right, though. With slightly more blue than yellow, it&#8217;s a bit on the calmer side, but it still manages to possess a quiet energy.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#00b140"><strong>Green Screen</strong><br>Hex #00B140<br>RGB 0, 177, 64<br>CMYK 100, 0, 64, 31</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Android Green</h2>



<p>This green is officially categorized as a shade of chartreuse. It was originally used as the color for the Android robot logo. But as of 2019, the brand switched to an updated hex value. However, the logo still appears in the original Android Green in some places. Android Green is very similar to the color of pea soup.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#a4c639"><strong>Android Green</strong><br>Hex #A4C639<br>RGB 164, 198, 57<br>CMYK 17, 0, 71, 22</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Bitter Lemon</h2>



<p>Most of us associate lemons with bright yellow. However, this color is that of a bitter, very unripe lemon, so the greenish yellow color makes sense. Bitter Lemon is very similar in color to Pear, although it is just slightly more yellow.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#cae00d"><strong>Bitter Lemon</strong><br>Hex #CAE00D<br>RGB 202, 224, 13<br>CMYK 10, 0, 94, 12</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Wageningen Green</h2>



<p>This name may seem like a mouthful at first, but it&#8217;s the name of a Dutch university. Wageningen Green is simply one of the school&#8217;s official colors. It&#8217;s somewhat rare in that its CMYK values for blue and yellow are exactly the same, which makes it pleasantly bright yet balanced.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#34b233"><strong>Wageningen Green</strong><br>Hex #34B233<br>RGB 52, 178, 51<br>CMYK 71, 0, 71, 30</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Sap Green</h2>



<p>Sap Green is one of the colors that was based on a historical paint. Traditionally, Sap Green was made with ripe buckthorn berries. Newer versions of the color typically aren&#8217;t made with berries, but they are nearly identical in color to the original. Sap Green is a balanced green that looks mildly like olive.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#507d2a"><strong>Sap Green</strong><br>Hex #507D2A<br>RGB 80, 125, 42<br>CMYK 36, 0, 66, 51</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Old Moss Green</h2>



<p>This color is a brownish green with a vintage appeal. And as the name suggests, it is just about the color of old moss. Old Moss Green works well as a neutral, and it looks good paired with other darker shades of green.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#867e36"><strong>Old Moss Green</strong><br>Hex #867E36<br>RGB 134, 126, 54<br>CMYK 0, 6, 60, 47</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Slimy Green</h2>



<p>Slimy Green is another color whose name doesn&#8217;t sound particularly appealing. However, the color itself is promising. It&#8217;s a deep, rich green that offers plenty of presence despite not being especially dark or especially bright. It&#8217;s a great statement-making shade for logos.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#299617"><strong>Slimy Green</strong><br>Hex #299617<br>RGB 41, 150, 23<br>CMYK 73, 0, 85, 41</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Very Light Malachite Green</h2>



<p>Malachite is an unusual-looking greenish mineral that comes in a variety of shades. Very Light Malachite Green very closely matches the lightest shades of malachite. As a color, it closely resembles some of the variants of spring green. It&#8217;s ideal if you want a light, airy-looking green that isn&#8217;t quite as pale as mint.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#64e986"><strong>Very Light Malachite Green</strong><br>Hex #64E986<br>RGB 100, 233, 134<br>CMYK 57, 0, 42, 9</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Dark Spring Green</h2>



<p>Speaking of spring greens, this is one of the more unusual variants. Dark Spring Green is, as the name suggests, a darker version of Spring Green. But it&#8217;s so dark that most people likely wouldn&#8217;t consider it to be a spring green. Dark Spring Green looks very similar to Dartmouth Green, and it&#8217;s a good choice if you want a dark green but prefer to stay away from common options like Hunter Green.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#177245"><strong>Dark Spring Green</strong><br>Hex #177245<br>RGB 23, 114, 69<br>CMYK 80, 0, 39, 55</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Guppie Green</h2>



<p>In the world of show guppies, green is a rare and sought-after color. Luckily, at least Guppie Green is easily accessible for your next project. This cheerful light green is brighter than a spring green but not as bright as neon. It&#8217;s ideal for projects where you need a somewhat energetic color scheme.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#00ff7f"><strong>Guppie Green</strong><br>Hex #00FF7F<br>RGB 0, 255, 127<br>CMYK 100, 0, 50, 0</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Apple Green</h2>



<p>Despite the similar names, this is a different color from Granny Smith Apple. Apple Green is a little bit darker, and it closely resembles the color of green apples seen in cartoons.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#8db600"><strong>Apple Green</strong><br>Hex #8DB600<br>RGB 141, 182, 0<br>CMYK 23, 0, 100, 29</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Deep Green</h2>



<p>The name of Deep Green is largely self-explanatory. Its close blue/yellow balance makes it a fairly classic green, and the relatively high percentage of black gives it a &#8220;deeper&#8221; look, as if it were a deep pool of green. It manages to look deep without being overly dark.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#056608"><strong>Deep Green</strong><br>Hex #056608<br>RGB 5, 102, 8<br>CMYK 95, 0, 92, 60</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Hooker&#8217;s Green</h2>



<p>Hooker&#8217;s Green originally was a pigment designed by botanical illustrator William Hooker, who needed an accurate dark green to paint large amounts of foliage. It was made by combining gamboge and Prussian blue. The color is still often produced, although it&#8217;s rarely made with natural pigments.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#49796b"><strong>Hooker&#8217;s Green</strong><br>Hex #49796B<br>RGB 73, 121, 107<br>CMYK 40, 0, 12, 53</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Medium Sea Green</h2>



<p>Like Dark Sea Green, Medium Sea Green is a variant of the very popular Sea Green. This is a beautiful, jade-like green that looks a bit like clear, blue-green ocean water. The color is deep yet cool, making it very centering to look at.</p>



<p class="has-white-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#3cb371"><strong>Medium Sea Green</strong><br>Hex #3CB371<br>RGB 60, 179, 113<br>CMYK 66, 0, 37, 30</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Turquoise Green</h2>



<p>You probably know turquoise as a blue color, but turquoise green is a pretty and uncommon version. Turquoise Green is a very light bluish green. And as you can see from the CMYK values, it is mostly blue. However, the addition of some yellow and some black makes it a uniquely beautiful, pastel-like color.</p>



<p class="has-black-color has-text-color has-background" style="background-color:#a0d6b4"><strong>Turquoise Green</strong><br>Hex #A0D6B4<br>RGB 160, 214, 180<br>CMYK 25, 0, 16, 16</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading">Green Colors</h2>



<p>There are countless shades of green, so many that you can continuously discover a new variation every single day. The colors mentioned above are only a fraction of them, but there should still be plenty for you to choose from for your graphic design, website, or whatever your heart desires to use the colors for.</p>



<p>These colors can also be found in nature. Heres a visual list of&nbsp;<a href="https://www.color-meanings.com/things-that-are-green/">things that are green</a>.</p>

	/**
	 * Displays toast message from storage, it is used when the user is redirected after login
	 */
	if ( window.sessionStorage ) {
		$( window ).on( 'tcb_after_dom_ready', () => {
			const message = sessionStorage.getItem( 'tcb_toast_message' );

			if ( message ) {
				tcbToast( sessionStorage.getItem( 'tcb_toast_message' ), false );
				sessionStorage.removeItem( 'tcb_toast_message' );
			}
		} );
	}

	/**
	 * Displays toast message
	 *
	 * @param {string}   message  - message to display
	 * @param {Boolean}  error    - whether the message is an error or not
	 * @param {Function} callback - callback function to be called after the message is closed
	 */
	function tcbToast( message, error, callback ) {
		/* Also allow "message" objects */
		if ( typeof message !== 'string' ) {
			message = message.message || message.error || message.success;
		}
		if ( ! error ) {
			error = false;
		}
		TCB_Front.notificationElement.toggle( message, error ? 'error' : 'success', callback );
	}
} )( typeof ThriveGlobal === 'undefined' ? jQuery : ThriveGlobal.$j );
</script><style type="text/css" id="tve_notification_styles"></style>

			<span class="tve_tick thrv-svg-icon"></span>
		</div>

	</div>
